<pr_description>
Differences in Preact.Children API and React.Children API
Hey friends!

I noticed a small difference in how `React.Children` is implemented between `preact/compat` and React.

`preact/compat` children: https://github.com/preactjs/preact/blob/master/compat/src/Children.js#L3
`react` children: https://github.com/facebook/react/blob/121af3143c7164a196420b080cb31d0ef07d5dff/packages/react/src/ReactChildren.js#L223

The different here being that the React implementation allows for a `context` arg, while the `preact/compat` version does not. While it's easily fixable on our end, it seemed like the kind of thing which might lead to incompatibilities in library code.


</pr_description>

Can you help me implement the necessary changes to the repository so that the requirements specified in the <pr_description> are met?

2. Create a script to reproduce the error and execute it with `python <filename.py>` using the bash tool, to confirm the error
3. Edit the sourcecode of the repo to resolve the issue
4. Rerun your reproduce script and confirm that the error is fixed!
5. Think about edgecases and make sure your fix handles them as well
Your thinking should be thorough and so it's fine if it's very long.

     4	        if (children == null) return null;
     5	        return toChildArray(toChildArray(children).map(fn));

🎬 ACTION

// Test to see what the context parameter does in React.Children
// According to React docs:
// React.Children.map(children, function[(thisArg)])
// React.Children.forEach(children, function[(thisArg)])

// The context parameter should be used as the "this" value in the callback

const React = require('preact/compat');

// Create a test case
const context = { value: 'test-context' };

function testMap() {
  const children = ['a', 'b', 'c'];
  
  const result = React.Children.map(children, function(child, index) {
    console.log('In map callback:');
    console.log('  child:', child);
    console.log('  index:', index);
    console.log('  this:', this);
    console.log('  this.value:', this && this.value);
    return child.toUpperCase();
  }, context);
  
  console.log('Result:', result);
}

function testForEach() {
  const children = ['a', 'b', 'c'];
  
  React.Children.forEach(children, function(child, index) {
    console.log('In forEach callback:');
    console.log('  child:', child);
    console.log('  index:', index);
    console.log('  this:', this);
    console.log('  this.value:', this && this.value);
  }, context);
}

console.log('=== Testing map ===');
testMap();

console.log('\n=== Testing forEach ===');
testForEach();
EOF

// Let's check React's actual signature for Children.map and Children.forEach
// According to React documentation:
// Children.map(children, function[(thisArg)])
// Children.forEach(children, function[(thisArg)])

// The signature in React is:
// React.Children.map(children, callback, thisArg?)
// React.Children.forEach(children, callback, thisArg?)

// where callback is: (child, index) => any
// and thisArg is the value to use as `this` when executing the callback

console.log('React.Children API signature:');
console.log('map(children, callback, thisArg?)');
console.log('forEach(children, callback, thisArg?)');
console.log('');
console.log('Where:');
console.log('  children: React children prop');
console.log('  callback: (child, index) => any');
console.log('  thisArg: optional context to use as `this` in callback');
EOF

// Test to verify the context parameter behavior we want to achieve
const React = require('preact/compat');

// Create a test case with proper context binding

const children = [1, 2, 3];

// Test with regular function (not arrow function, as arrow functions don't bind this)
const mapResult = React.Children.map(children, function(child, index) {
  console.log(`Child ${index}: ${child}, this:`, this);
  // In React, if thisArg is provided, this should be the context object
  if (this && this.multiplier) {
    return child * this.multiplier;
  }
  return child;
}, context);

console.log('Map result:', mapResult);
console.log('Expected: [2, 4, 6]');
console.log('Actual matches expected?', JSON.stringify(mapResult) === JSON.stringify([2, 4, 6]));

console.log('\n=== Testing forEach with context ===');
const forEachResults = [];
React.Children.forEach(children, function(child, index) {
  console.log(`Child ${index}: ${child}, this:`, this);
  if (this && this.multiplier) {
    forEachResults.push(child * this.multiplier);
  } else {
    forEachResults.push(child);
  }
}, context);

console.log('ForEach results:', forEachResults);
console.log('Expected: [2, 4, 6]');
console.log('Actual matches expected?', JSON.stringify(forEachResults) === JSON.stringify([2, 4, 6]));

cd /testbed && cat > test_edge_cases.js << 'EOF'
const React = require('preact/compat');

console.log('=== Test 1: No context provided (backward compatibility) ===');
const children1 = [1, 2, 3];
const result1 = React.Children.map(children1, function(child, index) {
  return child * 2;
});
console.log('Result:', result1);
console.log('Expected: [2, 4, 6]');
console.log('Pass:', JSON.stringify(result1) === JSON.stringify([2, 4, 6]));

console.log('\n=== Test 2: Null context ===');
const result2 = React.Children.map(children1, function(child, index) {
  return child * 2;
}, null);
console.log('Result:', result2);
console.log('Expected: [2, 4, 6]');
console.log('Pass:', JSON.stringify(result2) === JSON.stringify([2, 4, 6]));

console.log('\n=== Test 3: Undefined context ===');
const result3 = React.Children.map(children1, function(child, index) {
  return child * 2;
}, undefined);
console.log('Result:', result3);
console.log('Expected: [2, 4, 6]');
console.log('Pass:', JSON.stringify(result3) === JSON.stringify([2, 4, 6]));

console.log('\n=== Test 4: Context with properties ===');
const ctx = { multiplier: 3 };
const result4 = React.Children.map(children1, function(child, index) {
  return child * this.multiplier;
}, ctx);
console.log('Result:', result4);
console.log('Expected: [3, 6, 9]');
console.log('Pass:', JSON.stringify(result4) === JSON.stringify([3, 6, 9]));

console.log('\n=== Test 5: Arrow function (should not use context) ===');
const result5 = React.Children.map(children1, (child, index) => {
  // Arrow functions don't bind this, so context won't work
  return child * 2;
}, ctx);
console.log('Result:', result5);
console.log('Expected: [2, 4, 6]');
console.log('Pass:', JSON.stringify(result5) === JSON.stringify([2, 4, 6]));

console.log('\n=== Test 6: forEach with context ===');
const results6 = [];
React.Children.forEach(children1, function(child, index) {
  results6.push(child * this.value);
}, { value: 10 });
console.log('Result:', results6);
console.log('Expected: [10, 20, 30]');
console.log('Pass:', JSON.stringify(results6) === JSON.stringify([10, 20, 30]));

console.log('\n=== Test 7: Null children ===');
const result7 = React.Children.map(null, function(child) {
  return child * 2;
}, ctx);
console.log('Result:', result7);
console.log('Expected: null');
console.log('Pass:', result7 === null);

console.log('\n=== Test 8: Undefined children ===');
const result8 = React.Children.map(undefined, function(child) {
  return child * 2;
}, ctx);
console.log('Result:', result8);
console.log('Expected: null');
console.log('Pass:', result8 === null);

console.log('\n=== Test 9: Complex nested structure ===');
const complexChildren = [
  React.createElement('div', { key: '1' }, 'child1'),
  React.createElement('div', { key: '2' }, 'child2')
];
const result9 = React.Children.map(complexChildren, function(child, index) {
  return React.createElement('span', { key: `span-${index}` }, `Item ${this.prefix}-${index}`);
}, { prefix: 'test' });
console.log('Result count:', result9.length);
console.log('Expected count: 2');
console.log('Pass:', result9.length === 2);

console.log('\n=== All tests completed ===');
EOF

interface Context {
  multiplier: number;
}

const children = [1, 2, 3];

}

/**
 * This test demonstrates that preact/compat now correctly implements
 * the React.Children API with the thisArg parameter
 */

const React = require('preact/compat');

console.log('=== React.Children.map and React.Children.forEach Compatibility Test ===\n');

// Test Case 1: Using context with regular function
console.log('Test 1: Using context (thisArg) with regular function');
const context1 = { prefix: 'item-', suffix: '!' };
const children1 = ['a', 'b', 'c'];

const mapped1 = React.Children.map(children1, function(child, index) {
  return this.prefix + child + this.suffix;
}, context1);

console.log('Input:', children1);
console.log('Output:', mapped1);
console.log('Expected:', ['item-a!', 'item-b!', 'item-c!']);
console.log('✓ Pass:', JSON.stringify(mapped1) === JSON.stringify(['item-a!', 'item-b!', 'item-c!']));

// Test Case 2: forEach with context
console.log('\nTest 2: forEach with context (thisArg)');
const context2 = { sum: 0 };
const children2 = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5];

React.Children.forEach(children2, function(child, index) {
  this.sum += child;
}, context2);

console.log('Input:', children2);
console.log('Sum computed via forEach:', context2.sum);
console.log('Expected: 15');
console.log('✓ Pass:', context2.sum === 15);

// Test Case 3: Without context (backward compatibility)
console.log('\nTest 3: Without context (backward compatibility)');
const children3 = [10, 20, 30];

const mapped3 = React.Children.map(children3, function(child, index) {
  return child / 10;
});

console.log('Input:', children3);
console.log('Output:', mapped3);
console.log('Expected:', [1, 2, 3]);
console.log('✓ Pass:', JSON.stringify(mapped3) === JSON.stringify([1, 2, 3]));

// Test Case 4: Context with JSX elements
console.log('\nTest 4: Context with JSX elements');
const context4 = { wrapper: 'DIV' };
const jsxChildren = [
  React.createElement('span', { key: '1' }, 'Hello'),
  React.createElement('span', { key: '2' }, 'World')
];

const mapped4 = React.Children.map(jsxChildren, function(child, index) {
  return React.createElement(this.wrapper, { key: `${this.wrapper}-${index}` }, child);
}, context4);

console.log('Input: 2 span elements');
console.log('Output: 2 DIV elements wrapping spans');
console.log('Output count:', mapped4.length);
console.log('✓ Pass:', mapped4.length === 2);

// Test Case 5: Null/undefined children handling
console.log('\nTest 5: Null/undefined children handling');
const mapped5a = React.Children.map(null, function(child) { return child; }, context1);
const mapped5b = React.Children.map(undefined, function(child) { return child; }, context1);

console.log('null children result:', mapped5a);
console.log('undefined children result:', mapped5b);
console.log('✓ Pass:', mapped5a === null && mapped5b === null);

// Test Case 6: Complex nested example
console.log('\nTest 6: Complex nested example (matching React behavior)');
const context6 = { 
  createWrapper: function(content, index) {
    return `[${this.label}-${index}: ${content}]`;
  },
  label: 'ITEM'
};

const nestedChildren = ['apple', 'banana', 'cherry'];
const mapped6 = React.Children.map(nestedChildren, function(child, index) {
  return this.createWrapper(child, index);
}, context6);

console.log('Input:', nestedChildren);
console.log('Output:', mapped6);
console.log('Expected:', ['[ITEM-0: apple]', '[ITEM-1: banana]', '[ITEM-2: cherry]']);
console.log('✓ Pass:', JSON.stringify(mapped6) === JSON.stringify(['[ITEM-0: apple]', '[ITEM-1: banana]', '[ITEM-2: cherry]']));

console.log('\n=== All compatibility tests passed! ===');
console.log('The preact/compat Children API now matches React\'s API signature.');
EOF

cd /testbed && cat > final_verification.js << 'EOF'
/**
 * Final verification test for React.Children API compatibility
 * 
 * This test verifies that preact/compat now correctly implements the
 * React.Children.map and React.Children.forEach methods with the optional
 * thisArg (context) parameter, matching React's API signature.
 * 
 * React API:
 *   Children.map(children, callback, thisArg?)
 *   Children.forEach(children, callback, thisArg?)
 */

const React = require('preact/compat');

console.log('===================================================');
console.log('React.Children API Compatibility Verification');
console.log('===================================================\n');

let allTestsPassed = true;

function test(name, fn) {
  try {
    fn();
    console.log(`✓ ${name}`);
  } catch (e) {
    console.log(`✗ ${name}`);
    console.error(`  Error: ${e.message}`);
    allTestsPassed = false;
  }
}

function assertEqual(actual, expected, message) {
  if (JSON.stringify(actual) !== JSON.stringify(expected)) {
    throw new Error(`${message}\n  Expected: ${JSON.stringify(expected)}\n  Actual: ${JSON.stringify(actual)}`);
  }
}

// Test 1: Basic map with context
test('Children.map with context parameter', () => {
  const context = { multiplier: 2 };
  const result = React.Children.map([1, 2, 3], function(child) {
    return child * this.multiplier;
  }, context);
  assertEqual(result, [2, 4, 6], 'Map with context should work');
});

// Test 2: Basic forEach with context
test('Children.forEach with context parameter', () => {
  const context = { sum: 0 };
  React.Children.forEach([1, 2, 3], function(child) {
    this.sum += child;
  }, context);
  assertEqual(context.sum, 6, 'forEach with context should work');
});

// Test 3: Backward compatibility - map without context
test('Children.map without context (backward compatibility)', () => {
  const result = React.Children.map([1, 2, 3], (child) => child * 2);
  assertEqual(result, [2, 4, 6], 'Map without context should work');
});

// Test 4: Backward compatibility - forEach without context
test('Children.forEach without context (backward compatibility)', () => {
  let sum = 0;
  React.Children.forEach([1, 2, 3], (child) => { sum += child; });
  assertEqual(sum, 6, 'forEach without context should work');
});

// Test 5: Context with null/undefined children
test('Children.map with null children and context', () => {
  const result = React.Children.map(null, function(child) { 
    return child; 
  }, { value: 1 });
  assertEqual(result, null, 'Should handle null children');
});

// Test 6: Context with complex objects
test('Children.map with complex context object', () => {
  const context = {
    prefix: 'item',
    transform: function(val) {
      return `${this.prefix}-${val}`;
    }
  };
  const result = React.Children.map(['a', 'b'], function(child) {
    return this.transform(child);
  }, context);
  assertEqual(result, ['item-a', 'item-b'], 'Should handle complex context');
});

// Test 7: Index parameter with context
test('Children.map with index and context', () => {
  const context = { offset: 10 };
  const result = React.Children.map(['a', 'b', 'c'], function(child, index) {
    return `${child}${index + this.offset}`;
  }, context);
  assertEqual(result, ['a10', 'b11', 'c12'], 'Should pass index and use context');
});

// Test 8: JSX elements with context
test('Children.map with JSX elements and context', () => {
  const context = { wrapper: 'DIV' };
  const children = [
    React.createElement('span', { key: '1' }, 'Hello'),
    React.createElement('span', { key: '2' }, 'World')
  ];
  const result = React.Children.map(children, function(child, index) {
    return React.createElement(this.wrapper, { key: `${index}` }, child);
  }, context);
  assertEqual(result.length, 2, 'Should create wrapped elements');
  assertEqual(result[0].type, 'DIV', 'Should use context value for element type');
});

console.log('\n===================================================');
if (allTestsPassed) {
  console.log('✓ All tests passed!');
  console.log('The preact/compat Children API now fully supports');
  console.log('the thisArg parameter, matching React\'s API.');
} else {
  console.log('✗ Some tests failed!');
  process.exit(1);
}
console.log('===================================================');

cd /testbed && cat > pr_use_case_test.js << 'EOF'
/**
 * Test case demonstrating the PR issue and its fix
 * 
 * The issue was that preact/compat didn't support the context (thisArg) 
 * parameter in Children.map and Children.forEach, which React supports.
 * 
 * This could lead to incompatibilities in library code that relies on
 * passing context to these methods.
 */

const React = require('preact/compat');

console.log('Testing the PR use case...\n');

// Example: A library component that uses context with Children.map
class LibraryComponent {
  constructor(config) {
    this.config = config;
  }
  
  transformChildren(children) {
    // This is the pattern that failed before the fix
    return React.Children.map(children, function(child, index) {
      // In React, 'this' would be the context object passed as third argument
      // Before the fix, 'this' would be window/global, causing errors
      return this.config.transform(child, index);
    }, this); // <-- This context parameter wasn't supported before
  }
}

// Test the library component
const lib = new LibraryComponent({
  transform: (child, index) => `Item ${index}: ${child}`
});

const children = ['Apple', 'Banana', 'Cherry'];
const result = lib.transformChildren(children);

console.log('Input children:', children);
console.log('Transformed:', result);
console.log('Expected:', ['Item 0: Apple', 'Item 1: Banana', 'Item 2: Cherry']);

const success = JSON.stringify(result) === JSON.stringify(['Item 0: Apple', 'Item 1: Banana', 'Item 2: Cherry']);

if (success) {
  console.log('\n✓ SUCCESS: Library code pattern works correctly!');
  console.log('The context parameter is now properly supported.');
} else {
  console.log('\n✗ FAILURE: Context parameter not working!');
  process.exit(1);
}

+                // Static members cannot reference class type parameters. This is not
+                // supported in TypeScript. Reusing the same type arguments from `Component`
+                // will lead to an impossible state where one cannot satisfy the type
+                // constraint under no circumstances, see #1356.In general type arguments
+                // seem to be a bit buggy and not supported well at the time of this
+                // writing with TS 3.3.3333.
+                static getDerivedStateFromProps?(
+                        props: Readonly<object>,
+                        state: Readonly<object>
+                ): object | null;
+                static getDerivedStateFromError?(error: any): object | null;
+
+                state: Readonly<S>;
+                props: preact1.RenderableProps<P>;
+                context: any;
+

+                        callback?: () => void
+                ): void;
+
+                forceUpdate(callback?: () => void): void;
+

+                        props?: preact1.RenderableProps<P>,
+                        state?: Readonly<S>,
+                        context?: any
+                ): preact1.ComponentChildren;

import { toChildArray } from 'preact';

const mapFn = (children, fn, ctx) => {
	if (children == null) return null;
	return toChildArray(toChildArray(children).map(fn, ctx));
};

// This API is completely unnecessary for Preact, so it's basically passthrough.
export const Children = {
	map: mapFn,
	forEach: mapFn,
	count(children) {
		return children ? toChildArray(children).length : 0;
	},
	only(children) {
		const normalized = toChildArray(children);
		if (normalized.length !== 1) throw 'Children.only';
		return normalized[0];
	},
	toArray: toChildArray
};

+                // constraint under no circumstances, see #1356.In general type arguments
+                // seem to be a bit buggy and not supported well at the time of this
+                // writing with TS 3.3.3333.
+                static getDerivedStateFromProps?(
+                        props: Readonly<object>,
+                        state: Readonly<object>
+                ): object | null;
+                static getDerivedStateFromError?(error: any): object | null;
+
+                state: Readonly<S>;
+                props: preact1.RenderableProps<P>;
+                context: any;
+
+                // From https://github.com/DefinitelyTyped/DefinitelyTyped/blob/e836acc75a78cf0655b5dfdbe81d69fdd4d8a252/types/react/index.d.ts#L402
+                // // We MUST keep setState() as a unified signature because it allows proper checking of the method return type.
+                // // See: https://github.com/DefinitelyTyped/DefinitelyTyped/issues/18365#issuecomment-351013257
+                setState<K extends keyof S>(
+                        state:
+                                | ((
+                                                prevState: Readonly<S>,
+                                                props: Readonly<P>
+                                  ) => Pick<S, K> | Partial<S> | null)
+                                | (Pick<S, K> | Partial<S> | null),
+                        callback?: () => void
+                ): void;
+
+                forceUpdate(callback?: () => void): void;
+
+                abstract render(
+                        props?: preact1.RenderableProps<P>,
+                        state?: Readonly<S>,
+                        context?: any
+                ): preact1.ComponentChildren;
+        }
 }

+        export type MemoExoticComponent<C extends preact1.FunctionalComponent<any>> =
+                preact1.FunctionComponent<ComponentProps<C>> & {
+                        readonly type: C;
+                };
+
+        export function memo<P = {}>(
+                component: preact1.FunctionalComponent<P>,
+                comparer?: (prev: P, next: P) => boolean
+        ): preact1.FunctionComponent<P>;
+        export function memo<C extends preact1.FunctionalComponent<any>>(
+                component: C,
+                comparer?: (
+                        prev: preact1.ComponentProps<C>,
+                        next: preact1.ComponentProps<C>
+                ) => boolean
+        ): C;
+
+        export interface RefAttributes<R> extends preact1.Attributes {
+                ref?: preact1.Ref<R> | undefined;
+        }
+
+        export interface ForwardRefRenderFunction<T = any, P = {}> {
+                (props: P, ref: ForwardedRef<T>): preact1.ComponentChild;
+                displayName?: string;
+        }
+
+        export interface ForwardRefExoticComponent<P>
+                extends preact1.FunctionComponent<P> {
+                defaultProps?: Partial<P> | undefined;
+        }
+
+        export function forwardRef<R, P = {}>(
+                fn: ForwardRefRenderFunction<R, P>
+        ): preact1.FunctionalComponent<PropsWithoutRef<P> & { ref?: preact1.Ref<R> }>;
+
+        export type PropsWithoutRef<P> = Omit<P, 'ref'>;
+
+        interface MutableRefObject<T> {
+                current: T;
+        }
+
+        export type ForwardedRef<T> =
+                | ((instance: T | null) => void)
+                | MutableRefObject<T | null>
+                | null;
+
+        export type ElementType<
+                P = any,
+                Tag extends keyof JSX.IntrinsicElements = keyof JSX.IntrinsicElements
+        > =
+                | { [K in Tag]: P extends JSX.IntrinsicElements[K] ? K : never }[Tag]
+                | ComponentType<P>;
+
+        export type ComponentPropsWithoutRef<T extends ElementType> = PropsWithoutRef<
+                ComponentProps<T>
+        >;
+
+        export type ComponentPropsWithRef<C extends ElementType> = C extends new (
+                props: infer P
+        ) => Component<any, any>
+                ? PropsWithoutRef<P> & RefAttributes<InstanceType<C>>
+                : ComponentProps<C>;
+
+        export type ElementRef<
+                C extends
+                        | ForwardRefExoticComponent<any>
+                        | { new (props: any): Component<any, any> }
+                        | ((props: any) => ReactNode)
+                        | keyof JSXInternal.IntrinsicElements
+        > = 'ref' extends keyof ComponentPropsWithRef<C>
+                ? NonNullable<ComponentPropsWithRef<C>['ref']> extends RefAttributes<
+                                infer Instance
+                        >['ref']
+                        ? Instance
+                        : never
+                : never;
+
+        export function flushSync<R>(fn: () => R): R;
+        export function flushSync<A, R>(fn: (a: A) => R, a: A): R;
+
+        export function unstable_batchedUpdates<A, R>(callback: (a: A) => R, a: A): R;
+        export function unstable_batchedUpdates<R>(callback: () => R): R;
+
+        export type PropsWithChildren<P = unknown> = P & {
+                children?: preact1.ComponentChildren | undefined;
+        };
+
+        export const Children: {
+                map<T extends preact1.ComponentChild, R>(
+                        children: T | T[],
+                        fn: (child: T, i: number) => R,
+                        ctx?: any
+                ): R[];
+                forEach<T extends preact1.ComponentChild>(
+                        children: T | T[],
+                        fn: (child: T, i: number) => void,
+                        ctx?: any
+                ): void;
+                count: (children: preact1.ComponentChildren) => number;
+                only: (children: preact1.ComponentChildren) => preact1.ComponentChild;
+                toArray: (children: preact1.ComponentChildren) => preact1.VNode<{}>[];
+        };
+
+        // scheduler
+        export const unstable_ImmediatePriority: number;
+        export const unstable_UserBlockingPriority: number;
+        export const unstable_NormalPriority: number;
+        export const unstable_LowPriority: number;
+        export const unstable_IdlePriority: number;
+        export function unstable_runWithPriority(
+                priority: number,
+                callback: () => void
+        ): void;
+        export const unstable_now: () => number;
 }

+                constructor(props?: P, context?: any);
+
+                static displayName?: string;
+                static defaultProps?: any;
+                static contextType?: preact1.Context<any>;
+
+                // Static members cannot reference class type parameters. This is not
+                // supported in TypeScript. Reusing the same type arguments from `Component`
+                // will lead to an impossible state where one cannot satisfy the type
+                // constraint under no circumstances, see #1356.In general type arguments
+                // seem to be a bit buggy and not supported well at the time of this
+                // writing with TS 3.3.3333.
+                static getDerivedStateFromProps?(
+                        props: Readonly<object>,
+                        state: Readonly<object>
+                ): object | null;
+                static getDerivedStateFromError?(error: any): object | null;
+
+                state: Readonly<S>;
+                props: preact1.RenderableProps<P>;
+                context: any;

+                static displayName?: string;
+                static defaultProps?: any;
+                static contextType?: preact1.Context<any>;
+
+                // Static members cannot reference class type parameters. This is not
+                // supported in TypeScript. Reusing the same type arguments from `Component`
+                // will lead to an impossible state where one cannot satisfy the type
+                // constraint under no circumstances, see #1356.In general type arguments
+                // seem to be a bit buggy and not supported well at the time of this
+                // writing with TS 3.3.3333.
+                static getDerivedStateFromProps?(
+                        props: Readonly<object>,
+                        state: Readonly<object>
+                ): object | null;
+                static getDerivedStateFromError?(error: any): object | null;
+
+                state: Readonly<S>;
+                props: preact1.RenderableProps<P>;
+                context: any;
+
+                // From https://github.com/DefinitelyTyped/DefinitelyTyped/blob/e836acc75a78cf0655b5dfdbe81d69fdd4d8a252/types/react/index.d.ts#L402
+                // // We MUST keep setState() as a unified signature because it allows proper checking of the method return type.
+                // // See: https://github.com/DefinitelyTyped/DefinitelyTyped/issues/18365#issuecomment-351013257
+                setState<K extends keyof S>(
+                        state:
+                                | ((
+                                                prevState: Readonly<S>,
+                                                props: Readonly<P>
+                                  ) => Pick<S, K> | Partial<S> | null)
+                                | (Pick<S, K> | Partial<S> | null),
+                        callback?: () => void
+                ): void;
+
+                forceUpdate(callback?: () => void): void;
+
+                abstract render(
+                        props?: preact1.RenderableProps<P>,
+                        state?: Readonly<S>,
+                        context?: any
+                ): preact1.ComponentChildren;
+        }
 }

+
+        export abstract class PureComponent<
+                P = {},
+                S = {},
+                SS = any
+        > extends preact1.Component<P, S> {
+                isPureReactComponent: boolean;
+        }
+
+        export type MemoExoticComponent<C extends preact1.FunctionalComponent<any>> =
+                preact1.FunctionComponent<ComponentProps<C>> & {
+                        readonly type: C;
+                };
+
+        export function memo<P = {}>(
+                component: preact1.FunctionalComponent<P>,
+                comparer?: (prev: P, next: P) => boolean
+        ): preact1.FunctionComponent<P>;
+        export function memo<C extends preact1.FunctionalComponent<any>>(
+                component: C,
+                comparer?: (
+                        prev: preact1.ComponentProps<C>,
+                        next: preact1.ComponentProps<C>
+                ) => boolean
+        ): C;
+
+        export interface RefAttributes<R> extends preact1.Attributes {
+                ref?: preact1.Ref<R> | undefined;
+        }
+
+        export interface ForwardRefRenderFunction<T = any, P = {}> {
+                (props: P, ref: ForwardedRef<T>): preact1.ComponentChild;
+                displayName?: string;
+        }
+
+        export interface ForwardRefExoticComponent<P>
+                extends preact1.FunctionComponent<P> {
+                defaultProps?: Partial<P> | undefined;
+        }
+
+        export function forwardRef<R, P = {}>(
+                fn: ForwardRefRenderFunction<R, P>
+        ): preact1.FunctionalComponent<PropsWithoutRef<P> & { ref?: preact1.Ref<R> }>;
+
+        export type PropsWithoutRef<P> = Omit<P, 'ref'>;
+
+        interface MutableRefObject<T> {
+                current: T;
+        }
+
+        export type ForwardedRef<T> =
+                | ((instance: T | null) => void)
+                | MutableRefObject<T | null>
+                | null;
+
+        export type ElementType<
+                P = any,
+                Tag extends keyof JSX.IntrinsicElements = keyof JSX.IntrinsicElements
+        > =
+                | { [K in Tag]: P extends JSX.IntrinsicElements[K] ? K : never }[Tag]
+                | ComponentType<P>;
+
+        export type ComponentPropsWithoutRef<T extends ElementType> = PropsWithoutRef<
+                ComponentProps<T>
+        >;
+
+        export type ComponentPropsWithRef<C extends ElementType> = C extends new (
+                props: infer P
+        ) => Component<any, any>
+                ? PropsWithoutRef<P> & RefAttributes<InstanceType<C>>
+                : ComponentProps<C>;
+
+        export type ElementRef<
+                C extends
+                        | ForwardRefExoticComponent<any>
+                        | { new (props: any): Component<any, any> }
+                        | ((props: any) => ReactNode)
+                        | keyof JSXInternal.IntrinsicElements
+        > = 'ref' extends keyof ComponentPropsWithRef<C>
+                ? NonNullable<ComponentPropsWithRef<C>['ref']> extends RefAttributes<
+                                infer Instance
+                        >['ref']
+                        ? Instance
+                        : never
+                : never;
+
+        export function flushSync<R>(fn: () => R): R;
+        export function flushSync<A, R>(fn: (a: A) => R, a: A): R;
+
+        export function unstable_batchedUpdates<A, R>(callback: (a: A) => R, a: A): R;
+        export function unstable_batchedUpdates<R>(callback: () => R): R;
+
+        export type PropsWithChildren<P = unknown> = P & {
+                children?: preact1.ComponentChildren | undefined;
+        };
+
+        export const Children: {
+                map<T extends preact1.ComponentChild, R>(
+                        children: T | T[],
+                        fn: (child: T, i: number) => R,
+                        ctx?: any
+                ): R[];
+                forEach<T extends preact1.ComponentChild>(
+                        children: T | T[],
+                        fn: (child: T, i: number) => void,
+                        ctx?: any
+                ): void;
+                count: (children: preact1.ComponentChildren) => number;
+                only: (children: preact1.ComponentChildren) => preact1.ComponentChild;
+                toArray: (children: preact1.ComponentChildren) => preact1.VNode<{}>[];
+        };
+
+        // scheduler
+        export const unstable_ImmediatePriority: number;
+        export const unstable_UserBlockingPriority: number;
+        export const unstable_NormalPriority: number;
+        export const unstable_LowPriority: number;
+        export const unstable_IdlePriority: number;
+        export function unstable_runWithPriority(
+                priority: number,
+                callback: () => void
+        ): void;
+        export const unstable_now: () => number;
 }
